< Text>
Burke Williams is a lovely facility and my deep tissue massage by Jodi was excellent. But the spa itself is overpriced and it's hit or miss in services: the previous massage and facial I got there were only okay. I think I paid more than $180 for a 50 minute deep tissue.

I went there early in the morning and was confused why I couldn't enter through the main mall entrance. I called the spa and the lady at the desk picked up and told me to hold. I held for 5 minutes before giving up and hanging up on her. I found the solution eventually by wandering around the building. Turns out you need to go around to the mission street bloomingdales entrance, find an intercom, tell security you're there, and they'll let you in so you can ride the elevator up.

To its credit, it's a great place for a girl's spa day. It has a large jacuzzi/pool area (bring swimsuits if you're shy or you can go in in the buff) and a nice sauna room. You can chat, but some people get annoyed and point to the "quiet" signs. It was surprisingly packed even early at 8 am in the morning. Snacks include extremely cucumber-y water everywhere in abundance and apples.

There's also a sample bar - where if you're cheap like me... you can fill up on products and give yourself a facial in the bathroom. I especially love the smell of their cleanser. The eye moisturizer pills up and didn't sit well under eyeshadow.<//Text>

<Time>1621385991199</Time>< Text>
I visited Doctor Park for a simple tooth extraction. The first thing I noticed about his office is that they double book appointment times. This isn't that bad, I understand how some procedures are a quick in-n-out process. But his office knew weeks ahead of time that I was coming in for this extraction and still double booked. To make things worse he did not finish the job, left one root in. The only explanation he offered at the moment was that he simply didn't have time for it. His office referred me to another dentist that would not be able to see me for over a month later. By that time bone shards had begun to protrude from my gum causing discomfort. I understand that bone fragments are a normal part of the healing process but no one warned me about this when the referral for the next doctor was made. Now the dentist Dr. Park referred me to, who seemed rather surprised that Dr. Park sent me his way, is referring me to an oral surgeon in order to remove the root and clean up the bone fragments that were left behind. While all the staff and Dr. Park himself were very polite and professional, it does not matter much in the end if you do not finish the job and leave a bit of a mess behind.<//Text>

< Text>
These guys provided an amazing experience from the start of my new car search in January 2015 to the end of the hunt in June! Richard and Rosie were my initial points-of-contact; they provided a warm, welcoming experience and Richard was very patient as I moved from total indecision to well-researched shopper to satisfied lessee when he and Tony helped me settle on a brand new Mazda3. I absolutely love the car, but what makes it even more satisfying is the relationship that I've built with Culver City Mazda.

During my lengthy search I visited over 20 different dealerships in the LA area looking for the perfect car and every other place tried to hustle and pressure me into making a snap decision so they could get a quick sale. From the start, I could tell that Culver City Mazda was different. They operate at the highest level of integrity, which is why I came back there once I decided that a Mazda3 was the model that would best suit my lifestyle.

Everyone at this dealership was a joy to work with, from the receptionists on the phone to Will, the financing manager, to Richard and Tony. They know a lot about cars but they treated me with respect and never went "over my head" with car speak.

As we were hashing out the specifics of the lease, Tony and Will conducted themselves in a relaxed, confident and dignified demeanor; they answered all my questions plainly and didn't give me a run around, which is what I got pretty much everywhere else.

What made it even more attractive was the general workplace atmosphere. In the midst of an unimaginably hectic Saturday, with a lobby full of patrons and support technicians flying around, Tony Tehrani was the picture of calm, handling requests and treating everyone (co-workers, subordinates and potential customers) with the kind of respect we normally reserve for C-level executives.

I could go on and on and on about this place's excellence, but really you should go see for yourself. Truly EXCEPTIONAL!<//Text>

<Review>I purchased a vehicle here. It has turned out to be a good car for a fairly decent price. However, the product is not what I have issue with - the sales & service staff is why I am giving 2 stars. There was too much unnecessary deception & stress resulting from it.
Examples: 1) finding a vehicle (after the ones seen on their site were not there), test driving, deciding I like it, making an offer - then being told that the price given to me initially had been a 'mistake'...
2)then having to deal with the "certified pre-owned" certification not actually being completed up to Mazda standards,
3) bringing it back to the dealership and being lied to again,
4) having to call Mazda Corporate and get them involved
5) then take the vehicle to another dealership to have them confirm that several key points of the certification had not been done such as resetting the engine computer (which directly affects engine performance), broken wipers not fixed, very worn tires not being replaced...
And every time you call this place you end up getting transferred around to way way way too many people - all while being given excuses & very little help.  Since I purchased the car, I have met several people who had similar experiences wit this dealership.
Thankfully Mazda makes good vehicles and I have not had any problems with the actual car itself - only the shady antics of the sales & service teams at Culver City Mazda. They pretend, and even try in some instances, to be helpful - but frequently do not follow through, giving excuse after excuse why they cant help. < Review>
I purchased a new Mazda CX-5 from another dealer a few weeks ago, and yesterday noticed a clicking sound from one of the tires. When I inspected it, there was a nail puncturing the tire. I brought in my car to Culver City Mazda since it's actually the closest dealer to where I live.

They couldn't find a record of the pricey service plan that should cover this repair (I have to call the original dealer about this), but Ken in the service department offered to inspect it to see if it's something repairable.

Turns out it just needed a little plug, an $18 service. Since I recently purchased the car, he provided the service for free, and even threw in a car wash!  Remember that I purchased this car at a different dealer.

It was really a great experience, and if the purpose was to bring me back the next time I need service, it definitely worked. Everyone was very courteous and professional.  I brought it in early on a weekday morning and all in all it took about an hour which I felt was reasonable.

5 stars!</Review>
